## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a chemical species concentration as a function of time and current concentration. The rate law dA/dt typically depends on powers of A, and time dependence may arise from external forcing, intermediate coupling, or non-elementary mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 (constant consumption/production rate)
- First-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A (exponential decay/growth of concentration)
- Second-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction kinetics)
- nth-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate expression)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with equilibrium)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * A) (product-accelerated reaction)
- Logistic-type kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (1 + c1 * A) (self-limiting reaction)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with baseline)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type cooperative binding)
- Parallel pathways: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**c2 + c3 (multiple simultaneous reaction channels)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure power-law dependence on concentration (dA/dt ~ A^n) indicates an elementary reaction of order n — try integer and half-integer exponents first
- A constant additive term in the rate law suggests a zero-order source/sink or a reversible reaction approaching equilibrium
- Rational functions of A (e.g., A/(c+A)) indicate enzyme-like saturation where the rate plateaus at high concentration
- If dA/dt depends explicitly on t (not just through A), suspect time-varying external conditions such as temperature ramps, light intensity changes, or fed-batch addition
- Negative quadratic terms in A (e.g., c0*A - c1*A²) suggest autocatalytic or logistic behavior with a carrying capacity
- Square root dependence on A (A**0.5) often arises from radical chain mechanisms or dissociative equilibria
- Products of A with functions of t may indicate photochemical reactions with time-varying irradiation or catalytic deactivation
- Sign of the leading coefficient determines consumption (negative) vs. production (positive) — physical consistency requires dA/dt < 0 for simple decay when A > 0

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK15)

GT: -c0*sqrt(A) - c1*A*exp(-c2*_s*t) + c3*_t*sin(log(A + c4))

## Analysis

The GT expression is:
$$f(t, A) = -0.1207\sqrt{A} - 0.1207 A e^{-0.0686t} + 0.8537\sin(\log(A + 1))$$

This has three key structural components:
1. A $\sqrt{A}$ term (no time dependence)
2. An $A \cdot e^{-ct}$ term
3. A $\sin(\log(A+1))$ term (no time dependence)

Let me check each candidate for the ability to reproduce all three components, especially the crucial $\sin(\log(A+1))$ term.

**Key observation:** The $\sin(\log(A+1))$ term is highly distinctive. Very few candidates contain anything resembling this. Let me search for candidates that have $\sin(\log(...))$ or could produce it.

- **Candidates with sin(log(...))**: None of the candidates explicitly contain $\sin(\log(...))$.
- **Candidates with log(A+c)**: Candidates 2, 6, 17, 27, 41 have log terms, but these are plain $\log(...)$, not $\sin(\log(...))$.
- **Candidates with sin(...)**: Several candidates have $\sin(c \cdot t + c)$ or $\sin(A \cdot c + c)$ terms, but none have $\sin(\log(A+c))$.

Let me check candidate 27: $A c_0 e^{c_1 t} + A^{c_2} c_3 e^{c_4 t} + A^{c_5} c_6 \log(A c_7 + 1) + c_8$

This has $\log(A+c)$ but not $\sin(\log(A+c))$. Cannot match.

Candidate 17: $A c_0 e^{c_1 t} + A^{c_2} c_3 e^{c_4 t} + c_5 + c_6 \log(A^{c_7} c_8 + 1)$

Again, just $\log(...)$, not $\sin(\log(...))$.

Candidate 41: $A^{c_0} + c_1 t + c_2 e^{Ac_3} + c_4 e^{c_5 t} \log(Ac_6 + 1)$

This has $e^{c_5 t}\log(Ac_6+1)$, coupling time and the log term multiplicatively, which doesn't match the GT's time-independent $\sin(\log(A+1))$.

**Candidates with $\sin(A \cdot c + c)$**: Candidates 11, 23, 31 have $\sin(Ac + c)$, which is $\sin$ of a linear function of $A$, not $\sin(\log(A+c))$. These are fundamentally different functions.

**Candidates with cos(A)**: Several candidates (1, 3, 13, 24, 25, 37) have $\cos(A)$ terms. $\cos(A)$ is not equivalent to $\sin(\log(A+1))$.

**Candidate 40**: $A^{c_0} c_1 \sin(c_2 t + c_3) + A^{c_4} c_5 + c_6 e^{c_7 t}$

Setting $c_2 = 0$ makes the sin term time-independent: $c_1 \sin(c_3) A^{c_0}$, which becomes a power of $A$, not $\sin(\log(A+1))$.

**Candidate 36**: $A^{0.5} c_0 + A^{c_1} c_2 \sin(c_3 t + c_4) + c_5 e^{c_6 t} + c_7 e^{c_8 t}$

Has $\sqrt{A}$ and exponential decay, but the sin term is $\sin(c_3 t + c_4)$ which depends on $t$ only, not on $A$ in the way $\sin(\log(A+1))$ does. Setting $c_3=0$ makes it a constant times $A^{c_1}$, which can't produce $\sin(\log(A+1))$.

No candidate contains the structural element $\sin(\log(A + c))$, which is essential to match the GT. None of the available functional forms (power laws, exponentials, trigonometric functions of linear arguments, logarithms) can be combined to exactly equal $\sin(\log(A+1))$ for all values of $A$.

Conclusion: No match

I need to analyze each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.12072*sqrt(A) - 0.12072*A*exp(-0.06862*t) + 0.85374*sin(log(A + 1))`

The GT has three basis functions:
1. `sqrt(A)` — a term proportional to A^(1/2)
2. `A*exp(-0.06862*t)` — a term with A times a decaying exponential in t
3. `sin(log(A + 1))` — a sine of logarithm term

Let me check each candidate for structural compatibility.

### Candidate 1: `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + A^c2*c3 + c4 + c5*exp(c6*t)/A^(1/5) + c7*cos(A)/A^(1/5)`

Basis functions: `A*exp(c1*t)`, `A^c2`, constant, `exp(c6*t)/A^(1/5)`, `cos(A)/A^(1/5)`
GT needs `sin(log(A+1))`. `cos(A)/A^(1/5)` cannot match `sin(log(A+1))`. No `sqrt(A)` can be obtained from `A^c2` (set c2=0.5), but `sin(log(A+1))` is missing.
Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 2: `A^c0*c1*sin(c2*t + c3) + c4*log(A*c5 + 1) + c6*exp(c7*t)`

Basis: `A^c0*sin(c2*t+c3)`, `log(A*c5+1)`, `exp(c7*t)`
GT needs `sin(log(A+1))` which is not `log(A+1)`. GT needs `sqrt(A)` and `A*exp(t)`. The term `A^c0*sin(c2*t+c3)` mixes A and t in a product, but GT's sin term has no t-dependence (since _t is just a constant multiplier). Wait - let me re-read GT: `c3*_t*sin(log(A + c4))` = `0.85374*sin(log(A+1))`. This has no t-dependence.

For `A^c0*sin(c2*t+c3)`: if c2=0, this becomes `A^c0*c1*sin(c3)` = constant * A^c0, which could give sqrt(A). But then we lose the sin(log(A+1)) term. `log(A*c5+1)` ≠ `sin(log(A+1))`. Missing basis functions.
Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 3: `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + A^c2*c3 + A^c4*c5 + c6 + c7*exp(c8*t)/A^(1/5) + c9*cos(A)/A^(1/5)`
